كتاب الوصايا باب العتق في المرض والوصية بالعتق
يوم
جميعاً متى اختار المسلم إليه المضي في السلم أنه يرد ثلث رأس المال إلى رب السلم حتى ينقسم ثلث المال على المحابتين جميعاً ينقض السلم في الثلث، فإذا دخل الأجل وأدى المسلم إليه سدس الطعام ويسترد منه نصف الثلث من رأس المال لأنه بحلول الأجل ذهب بالمحاباة في الأجل وبقيت المحاباة في الثمن، ومتى استرد نصف الثلث تنقض الإقالة في السلم بعد استقرارها في رأس المال وأنه لا يجوز فلهذه الضرورة تعذر اعتبار المحاباة بالأجل مع المحاباة بالثمن فكان إلغاء المحاباة بالأجل أولى لأنه بيع، وإذا لغت المحاباة بالأجل صار كأنه حابي بالثمن لا غير فيخير. وإذا أسلم المريض عشرة دراهم في كر يساوي عشرين ثم أقاله ثم مات جازت الإقالة في ثلثي الكر ويقال للمسلم إليه أدَّ ثلث الكر ورد عليهم ثلثي رأس المال لأن المحاباة في مرض الموت وصية والوصية معتبرة في الثلث ولو أسلم عشرة دراهم في كر يساوي ثلاثين درهماً وقد حابي بعشرين والعشرة من عشرين قدر نصفه، ولو أخذ منه رأس المال وأنفقه جازت الإقالة في ثلث الكر وبطلت في ثلثيه ويقال للمسلم إليه أذ إلى الورثة ثلثي الكر وارجع عليهم بثلثي العشرة لأن ثلث ماله مثل ثلث المحاباة لأن ماله القسمة ستة دراهم وثلاثين وقد حاباه بعشرين فيكون ثلث ماله مثل ثلث المحاباة فتجوز الإقالة في ثلثي الكر وبطلت في ثلثه فرد المسلم إليه إلى الورثة ثلثي الكر وقيمته عشرون إلا أن على رب السلم ستة دراهم وثلاثين ديناً لأنه قبض عشرة دراهم من المسلم إليه رأس المال ثلثه بحق جواز في ثلثي الكر وثلثه بغير حق لبطلان الإقالة في ثلثي الكر وقد استهلكها فصار ذلك ديناً عليه والإقالة قبل قبض السلم وبعده سواء عندهما، وعند أبي حنيفة هو بعد لما عرف أن الإقالة فسخ عندهما، وعنده بيع جديد. وإذا اشترى في مرضه عبداً قيمته مائة بخمسين دهماً فلم يتقابضا حتى تقايلا البيع فالبائع بالخيار إن شاء رد العبد وأخذ ثمنه وبطلت الإقالة وإن شاء سلم لهم ثلث العبد وأخذ منهم ثلث الخمسين لأن ثلث المال مثل ثلث المحاباة لأن ثلث المال المشتري ثلاثة وثلاثون وثلث لأن ماله عند قسمته مائة وقد حابي بخمسين فتجوز الإقالة في ثلثي العبد ولا تجوز في ثلثه، ثم يخير بين فسخ الإقالة أن وبين يجيزه زه أو لم يجيزه في السلم لأن الإقالة في البيع تحتمل الفسخ ما دام المعقود عليه قائماً، وفي السلم لا تحتمل الفسخ لأنه لا يمكن أن يجعل بيعاً مستقلاً لأن الاستدلال بالمسلم فيه قبل القبض لا يجوز .
القبض ابتداء بيع
ولو أسلم عشرين درهماً في كر يساوي عشرة في مرضه وله على الناس ديون فلم يخرج حتى أبطل القاضي السلم أو أعطى الكل ورد سدس رأس المال ثم خرج الدين جاز ذلك ولم يرد على المسلم إليه شيء إلا أن يخرج الدين قبل أن يختصموا فإن خرج مقدار ما يخرج سلم له المحاباة لأن المحاباة عشرة لأن ماله العين عشرون درهماً والدين لا يعد مال الميت ما لم يقض لأنه قد لا يخرج فيكون ثلث ماله ستة دراهم وثلثان فتصح المحاباة
من الثلث
بقدر ويتخير بين الفسخ والمضي لأن السلم يحتمل الفسخ وقد تعين على المسلم إليه شرط عقده فيتخير، فإذا أبى المسلم إليه الفسخ ونقض القاضي فإنه لا ينتقض النقض بعد ذلك، فإن زال السبب المقتضي للنقض وهو عدم خروج المحاباة من ثلث ماله لأن القضاء بالنقض لا يحتمل البطلان كما لو قضى بفسخ البيع بسبب العيب ثم زال العيب لا يعود البيع، وإن زال المقتضي للفسخ وهو العيب فكذا هذا وإن خرج من الدين قبل النقض مقدار ما يخرج المحاباة من الثلث سلم له المحاباة لأن الدين بالقبض صار عيناً فيعتبر ماله القسمة . وإذا
جميع
من
يوم
أسلم إلى مريض عشرة دراهم في كر يساوي أربعين فأنفق رأس المال ثم مات ولا مال له غير الكر فرب السلم بالخيار إن شاء نقض السلم ورجع على الورثة بدراهمه، وإن شار أخذ الكر وأعطى عشرين درهماً لأنه تغير عليه شرط عقده، فإن رضي أن يسلم له جميع الكر بعشرة دراهم والآن لا يسلم له الجميع بعشرة وعقده مما لا يحتمل الفسخ فيتخير، فإن مضى في السلم أخذ . الكر ورد عشرين لأن المسلم إليه حاباه بقدر ثلاثين فإنه باع ما يساوي أربعين بعشرة والمحاباة أكثر من ثلث ماله فتنفذ الوصية . الثلث ماله بعد الدين وجميع ثلاثون لأن عشرة من الكر مشغول بالعشرة التي استهلكها المسلم إليه فالمشغول بالدين لا يعدل مال الميت لأن الدين مقدم على الوصية والفارغ من الدين قدر ثلثين فيكون له عشرة بالوصية ويرد عشراً على الورثة ؛ هكذا ذكره الحاكم في مختصره. وذكر الفقيه أبو بكر البلخي في وجيزه أنه متى اختار المضي يأخذ نصف الكر ويترك النصف لأنه يكون لرب السلم نصف الكر قيمته عشرون عشرة منها تعوض ما قبض وهو رأس المال وعشره بغير عوض ثلث مال الميت والصحيح ما ذكر الحاكم لأن في هذا تبعيض على ورثة المسلم بالمحاباة وهو إليه بغير رضاهم وهذا لا يجوز كما في العبد والثوب الواحد فإن كان على الميت دين يحيط بتركته لم تجز المحاباة في التركة لأن المحاباة في المرض وصية والوصية تنفذ ثلث المال من الفارغ عن الدين ولم يوجد ولو أسلم إلى مريض عشرة في كر قيمته مائة فقبض رأس المال وأنفقه ومات وقد أوصى بثلث ماله فإن شاء رب السلم نقض السلم وأخذ دراهمه ويجوز للآخر وصيته، وإن شاء أخذ الكر وأعطى الورثة ستين درهماً ولا شيء لصاحب الوصية في قول أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يتحاصان في الثلث يضرب فيه رب السلم بتسعين وصاحب الوصية بثلاثين وهو ثلث المال فيكون الثلث بينهما على أربعة فيأخذ رب السلم الكر ويؤدي سبعة وستين درهماً ونصف منها تسعة الثلث لصاحب الوصية. وتخريجه أن عند أبي حنيفة ربع المحاباة أولى من الوصية ومال الميت قيمته مائة إلا أن عشرة منها مشغولة بالدين فيبقى ماله الفارغ بين رب السلم والموصى له على أربعة لأن الوصية بالمحاباة وصية ماله وذلك بجميع تسعون والوصية الأخرى بالثلث وذلك ثلاثون فيقسم الثلث على سبيل العول عندهما على أربعة ثلاثة أرباعه لصاحب المحاباة وذلك ثلاث وعشرون ونصف وأربعة للموصى له
Book of Bequests, Chapter of Manumission in Illness and Bequest of Manumission. Day altogether. Whenever the party to whom the salam is made chooses to proceed with the salam, he returns one-third of the capital to the salam giver so that one-third of the wealth is divided between the two favors. The salam is rescinded in one-third. When the term arrives and the recipient delivers one-sixth of the food, he recovers half of the third of the capital because with the term the favor in the term is gone and the favor in the price remains. When he recovers half of the third, the iqala in the salam is rescinded after it had been established in the capital, and it is not permissible. For this necessity, considering the favor in the term together with the favor in the price becomes impossible, so canceling the favor in the term is more appropriate because it is a sale. When the favor in the term is canceled, it becomes as if he favored only in the price, so he may choose. If a sick person gives ten dirhams as salam for a kurr worth twenty, then cancels (iqala), then dies: the iqala is valid for two-thirds of the kurr, and it is said to the recipient: deliver one-third of the kurr and return two-thirds of the capital. Because the favor (muhabah) in illness is a bequest, and a bequest is considered from one-third. If he gave ten dirhams for a kurr worth thirty, and he favored by twenty, and ten out of twenty is half. If he took the capital and spent it, the iqala is valid for one-third of the kurr and void for two-thirds. It is said to the recipient: deliver two-thirds of the kurr to the heirs and demand from them two-thirds of ten, because one-third of his wealth is like one-third of the favor. Because his wealth in division is thirty-six dirhams, and he favored by twenty, so one-third of his wealth equals one-third of the favor. Thus the iqala is valid for two-thirds of the kurr and void for one-third. So the recipient gives the heirs two-thirds of the kurr worth twenty, except that the salam-giver owes thirty-six dirhams because he received ten dirhams from the recipient as capital. One-third of it is rightfully for validity in two-thirds of the kurr, and one-third is without right due to voidness of iqala in two-thirds of the kurr, and he has consumed it, so that becomes a debt upon him. The iqala before and after taking possession of the salam is the same according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Abu Hanifa, it is after, because it is known that iqala is rescission according to them, and according to him it is a new sale. If a sick person buys a slave worth one hundred for fifty dirhams, and they have not exchanged possession until they mutually cancel the sale: the seller has the option: if he wishes, he returns the slave and takes his price, and the iqala becomes void; if he wishes, he delivers one-third of the slave to them and takes from them one-third of fifty, because one-third of the wealth is like one-third of the favor. Because the buyer's wealth when divided is one hundred, and he favored by fifty, so the iqala is valid for two-thirds of the slave and not valid for one-third. Then he may choose between annulling the iqala and approving it—whether he approved it or not in the salam. Because iqala in a sale can bear annulment as long as the object is still in existence; in salam it cannot bear annulment because it cannot be made an independent sale, since selling the salam commodity before taking possession is not allowed. Taking possession is an initial sale. If a sick person gives twenty dirhams as salam for a kurr worth ten, and he has debts owed to him by people, and these are not realized until the judge invalidates the salam, or gives the whole and returns one-sixth of the capital, then the debt comes out—that is permissible and nothing is returned to the recipient. Except if the debt comes out before they litigate: if it comes out to the amount that allows the favor to exit, the favor is valid for him. Because the favor is ten. His wealth in cash is twenty dirhams, and a debt is not considered the deceased's wealth until it is collected, because it may not come out. So one-third of his wealth is six and two-thirds, so the favor is valid from one-third. He may choose between annulment and proceeding, because the salam can bear annulment, and the condition of his contract has become specific to the recipient, so he may choose. If the recipient refuses the annulment and the judge annuls, that annulment is not afterwards annulled. If the cause that necessitated the annulment—namely the favor not coming out of one-third of his wealth—ceases, the judgment of annulment cannot bear being void, just as if a judge ruled to annul a sale due to a defect, then the defect ceases, the sale does not return. So here, if the cause of annulment (the defect) ceases, likewise. If the debt comes out before the annulment to the amount that allows the favor to come out from one-third, the favor is valid for him, because the debt upon receipt becomes cash, so his wealth is considered in division. And if a sick person receives salam: ten dirhams for a kurr worth forty, he spends the capital, then dies, and he has no wealth other than the kurr. The salam-giver has the option: if he wishes, he annuls the salam and demands his dirhams from the heirs; if he wishes, he takes the kurr and gives twenty dirhams, because the condition of his contract has changed for him. If he agreed that the entire kurr be given to him for ten dirhams, but now the entire kurr cannot be given for ten, and his contract does not bear annulment, so he may choose. If he proceeds with the salam, he takes the kurr and returns twenty, because the recipient favored him by thirty. Indeed, he sold what is worth forty for ten, and the favor exceeds one-third of his wealth, so the bequest is executed. One-third of his wealth after debt is thirty altogether, because ten of the kurr are occupied by the ten that the recipient consumed. That which is occupied by a debt is not counted as the deceased's wealth, because a debt takes precedence over a bequest. The part free from debt is two-thirds, so he gets ten by bequest and returns ten to the heirs. Thus mentioned al-Hakim in his Mukhtasar. Al-Faqih Abu Bakr al-Balkhi mentioned in his Wajiz that when he chooses to proceed, he takes half the kurr and leaves half, because the salam-giver gets half the kurr worth twenty: ten of it compensate what he received (the capital) and ten without compensation as one-third of the deceased's wealth. The correct is what al-Hakim mentioned, because in this opinion there is a partial allocation to the heirs of the deceased by the favor, which is done without their consent, and this is not permissible, just as with a single slave or garment. If the deceased has a debt covering all his estate, the favor is not valid in the estate, because the favor in illness is a bequest, and a bequest is executed from one-third of the wealth free from debt, and that does not exist. If a sick person gives salam: ten dirhams for a kurr worth one hundred, he takes the capital and spends it, then dies, and he has bequeathed one-third of his wealth. Then the salam-giver may annul the salam and take his dirhams, and the other's bequest is valid. Or he may take the kurr and give the heirs sixty dirhams, and nothing is for the testator according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), they share in the third: the salam-giver claims ninety and the testator claims thirty, which is one-third of the wealth. So the third is divided between them in four parts: the salam-giver takes the kurr and gives sixty-seven and a half dirhams, of which nine are the third for the testator. The reasoning is that according to Abu Hanifa, the bequest of the favor takes precedence over the (other) bequest. The deceased's wealth is one hundred, but ten of it are occupied by debt. So his free wealth is between the salam-giver and the legatee in four parts, because the bequest by favor is a bequest of his wealth, which totals ninety, and the other bequest is one-third, which is thirty. So one-third is divided by 'awl according to the two into four parts: three-fourths for the owner of the favor, which is twenty-three and a half, and one-fourth for the legatee.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a Hanafi commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discusses the rulings on salam (forward sale) and its cancellation (iqala) when the seller is terminally ill (marad al-mawt). The central principle is that any favor (muhabah) in a contract during terminal illness is treated as a bequest (wasiyyah), which is only valid up to one-third of the deceased's estate after debts are paid. The text examines several hypothetical scenarios to illustrate the application of this rule.

The first scenario: a sick person gives ten dirhams as salam for a kurr of wheat worth twenty dirhams, then cancels (iqala) and dies. Since the favor is ten dirhams, and it is a bequest, it must come from one-third of the estate. If the estate is thirty, one-third is ten, so the favor is all within the one-third, so the iqala is valid for the whole? Actually the text says the iqala is valid for two-thirds of the kurr. Let's follow: The deceased's wealth is not clearly stated. But the principle: the iqala is treated as a new sale at a reduced price; the reduction is the favor. So if the favor exceeds one-third, the iqala is partially void.

The text then mentions a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the nature of iqala: according to the Sahibayn, iqala is a rescission (faskh), so it is valid regardless of possession? According to Abu Hanifa, iqala is a new sale, so it is only valid after possession? The text clarifies that in salam, iqala before and after possession is the same according to the Sahibayn, but according to Abu Hanifa it is after possession only. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.

The passage also discusses situations where the salam-giver has a choice to either annul the iqala or proceed with partial execution, depending on whether the favor is within the one-third. If the deceased has other debts, those take precedence, and the bequest is from the residue.

A notable scenario: if a sick person buys a slave worth one hundred for fifty, then cancels before possession, the seller has options. The favor is fifty, which is half the price. The buyer's estate is one hundred, so one-third is about thirty-three. The favor of fifty exceeds one-third, so the iqala is valid only for two-thirds of the slave (since the favor in two-thirds is about thirty-three).

Another scenario: the deceased has a debt that is not yet collected. The debt is not considered part of the estate for bequest purposes until it is actually received, because it may not be collected. This affects the calculation of the one-third.

Finally, the passage compares the view of al-Hakim and Abu Bakr al-Balkhi on a specific case. The correct view is that of al-Hakim, because the alternative (Balkhi's) would result in a partial allocation of the favor to the heirs without their consent, which is impermissible.

This passage demonstrates the meticulous casuistry of Hanafi fiqh in applying the bequest rule to commercial transactions during terminal illness. It shows how the law balances the deceased's voluntary transactions against the rights of heirs.

Key Terms
الترجيح (al-tarjīḥ): Preferring one opinion over another based on strength of evidence or overarching principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario of 10 dirhams for a kurr worth 40, what is the correct distribution according to the passage?
A) The salam-giver takes half the kurr and leaves half.
B) The salam-giver takes the entire kurr and pays 20 dirhams.
C) The salam-giver takes the entire kurr and pays 10 dirhams.
D) The salam-giver takes the entire kurr and pays nothing.

Key Takeaway
When applying the one-third rule, debts must be deducted first; the correct view avoids giving the heirs part of the favor involuntarily.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
Salam During Terminal Illness: Buyer's Option and Mahaba Calculation
Explains buyer's option and mahaba calculation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that mahaba in a salam contract during terminal illness is treated as a bequest limited to one-third of the estate, and calculate the compensation due to heirs.

Core Idea
Excessive favor in a salam contract during illness is a bequest limited to one-third.

When a terminally ill person sells goods in a salam contract below market value, the buyer benefits from a favor (mahaba). Hanafi fiqh treats this favor as a bequest from the seller, and thus it is limited to one-third of the estate after debts. This lesson unpacks the buyer's options and the two scholarly methods for calculating the compensation owed to the heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the buyer's options
The buyer gave 10 dirhams in salam for a kurr worth 40. The seller spends the capital and dies, leaving only the kurr. The buyer can annul the contract and reclaim the capital from the heirs, or proceed with the contract and pay compensation for the excessive favor.
2
Understand the limit on mahaba
The mahaba (30 dirhams) is a bequest. Since it exceeds one-third of the estate (after debts), the excess must be compensated. The estate after debt is 30 dirhams (the kurr worth 40 minus 10 consumed capital), so one-third is 10 dirhams. Thus 10 dirhams of favor is valid, 20 must be repaid.
3
Compare the two calculation methods
Al-Hakim: buyer takes the whole kurr and returns 10 dirhams to heirs (the excess over one-third). Al-Balkhi: buyer takes half the kurr and leaves half. The passage favors al-Hakim because Balkhi's method imposes a division on heirs without consent.
4
Apply the rule to the case with full debt
If the seller's debt consumes the entire estate, there is no free portion; thus no mahaba is permitted, and the buyer must either annul or compensate the full favor.

Source Text

بقدر ويتخير بين الفسخ والمضي لأن السلم يحتمل الفسخ وقد تعين على المسلم إليه شرط عقده فيتخير، فإذا أبى المسلم إليه الفسخ ونقض القاضي فإنه لا ينتقض النقض بعد ذلك، فإن زال السبب المقتضي للنقض وهو عدم خروج المحاباة من ثلث ماله لأن القضاء بالنقض لا يحتمل البطلان كما لو قضى بفسخ البيع بسبب العيب ثم زال العيب لا يعود البيع، وإن زال المقتضي للفسخ وهو العيب فكذا هذا وإن خرج من الدين قبل النقض مقدار ما يخرج المحاباة من الثلث سلم له المحاباة لأن الدين بالقبض صار عيناً فيعتبر ماله القسمة . وإذا أسلم إلى مريض عشرة دراهم في كر يساوي أربعين فأنفق رأس المال ثم مات ولا مال له غير الكر فرب السلم بالخيار إن شاء نقض السلم ورجع على الورثة بدراهمه، وإن شاء أخذ الكر وأعطى عشرين درهماً لأنه تغير عليه شرط عقده، فإن رضي أن يسلم له جميع الكر بعشرة دراهم والآن لا يسلم له الجميع بعشرة وعقده مما لا يحتمل الفسخ فيتخير، فإن مضى في السلم أخذ الكر ورد عشرين لأن المسلم إليه حاباه بقدر ثلاثين فإنه باع ما يساوي أربعين بعشرة والمحاباة أكثر من ثلث ماله فتنفذ الوصية . الثلث ماله بعد الدين وجميع ثلاثون لأن عشرة من الكر مشغول بالعشرة التي استهلكها المسلم إليه فالمشغول بالدين لا يعدل مال الميت لأن الدين مقدم على الوصية والفارغ من الدين قدر ثلثين فيكون له عشرة بالوصية ويرد عشراً على الورثة ؛ هكذا ذكره الحاكم في مختصره. وذكر الفقيه أبو بكر البلخي في وجيزه أنه متى اختار المضي يأخذ نصف الكر ويترك النصف لأنه يكون لرب السلم نصف الكر قيمته عشرون عشرة منها تعوض ما قبض وهو رأس المال وعشرة بغير عوض ثلث مال الميت والصحيح ما ذكر الحاكم لأن في هذا تبعيض على ورثة المسلم بالمحاباة وهو إليه بغير رضاهم وهذا لا يجوز كما في العبد والثوب الواحد فإن كان على الميت دين يحيط بتركته لم تجز المحاباة في التركة لأن المحاباة في المرض وصية والوصية تنفذ ثلث المال من الفارغ عن الدين ولم يوجد
According to [the previous], and he chooses between annulment and continuation because salam can be annulled and the condition of his contract is binding on the Muslim ilayhi, so he has the choice. If the Muslim ilayhi refuses annulment and the judge annuls, then the annulment is not [itself] annulled afterwards. If the reason for annulment disappears – which is that the favor [mahaba] does not come from one-third of his wealth – because the judicial annulment does not admit of nullification, just as if a judge annuls a sale due to a defect and then the defect disappears, the sale does not return. And if the reason for annulment – the defect – disappears, so too this. And if before the annulment, an amount equal to the favor exits from debt, then the favor is valid for him because the debt, upon receipt, becomes a specific asset, so its division is considered. If someone gives a sick person ten dirhams as salam for a kurr worth forty, and he spends the capital, then dies with no property other than the kurr, then the salam buyer has the choice: if he wishes, he annuls the salam and takes back his dirhams from the heirs; if he wishes, he takes the kurr and gives twenty dirhams because the condition of his contract has changed. If he agrees to let him have the entire kurr for ten dirhams, now he does not get the entire [kurr] for ten, and his contract cannot be annulled, so he chooses. If he proceeds with the salam, he takes the kurr and returns twenty because the Muslim ilayhi favored him by thirty: he sold what is worth forty for ten, and the favor is more than one-third of his wealth, so the bequest is executed. One-third of his wealth after debt is thirty total, because ten of the kurr is occupied by the ten that the Muslim ilayhi consumed; the occupied by debt is not counted as the deceased's property because debt takes precedence over bequest, and the unoccupied [portion] is twenty, so he gets ten by bequest and returns ten to the heirs. Thus mentioned al-Hakim in his Mukhtasar. And al-Faqih Abu Bakr al-Balkhi mentioned in his Wajiz that whenever he chooses to proceed, he takes half the kurr and leaves half, because the salam buyer gets half the kurr worth twenty, ten of which compensate what he received – the capital – and ten without compensation, one-third of the deceased's wealth. The correct is what al-Hakim mentioned, because this imposes a division on the heirs regarding the favor, which is done without their consent, and this is not permissible, as in the case of a single slave or garment. If the deceased has a debt that encompasses his entire estate, the favor is not permissible in the estate because favor during illness is a bequest, and the bequest is executed from one-third of the wealth free of debt, and that does not exist.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage deals with a salam (advance purchase) transaction where the seller becomes terminally ill and dies, having spent the capital. The buyer has the option to either cancel the contract and reclaim the capital from the heirs, or to go ahead and take the goods while compensating the heirs for the excessive favor (mahaba) that exceeds one-third of the estate. The ruling turns on determining how much of the favor is permissible as a bequest (limited to one-third of the estate after debts). The author presents two views: al-Hakim's calculation gives the buyer the entire kurr and requires him to return ten dirhams, while al-Balkhi's calculation gives only half the kurr. The commentator prefers al-Hakim's view because it avoids imposing a division on the heirs without their consent. If the deceased's debt covers the entire estate, the favor is invalid since there is no free portion.

Key Terms
المحاباة (al-muḥābāh): The difference between the market value and the price paid in a transaction, treated as a gift or favor.
السلم (as-salam): An advance payment sale where the price is paid upfront for goods to be delivered later.
الثلث (ath-thulth): One-third of the estate, the maximum portion that can be bequeathed to non-heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the salam case where a sick person sells a kurr worth 40 for 10 and dies, according to al-Hakim, how much does the buyer pay to the heirs?
A) 0 dirhams
B) 10 dirhams
C) 20 dirhams
D) 30 dirhams

Key Takeaway
Mahaba in a salam contract during terminal illness is a bequest limited to one-third of the estate after debts; the buyer must compensate the heirs for any excess.

Prioritizing Mahaba Bequest Over Fractional Bequest: Abu Hanifa vs. the Two Companions
Intra-Hanafi dispute on bequest allocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's and the two companions' positions on the allocation of bequests when a mahaba favor competes with a separate one-third bequest, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to determine the practical outcome.

Core Idea
When two bequests compete within the one-third, Abu Hanifa prioritizes the mahaba bequest over a fractional bequest.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement: if a sick person sells a kurr worth 100 for 10 in salam, and also bequeaths one-third of his wealth, how do we allocate the one-third? Abu Hanifa gives the salam buyer the entire one-third; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad split it proportionally. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the principle that bequests in specific assets can override fractional bequests.

Guided Path
1
Identify the facts of the case
A sick person receives 10 dirhams as salam for a kurr worth 100, takes the capital and spends it, then dies leaving a separate bequest of one-third of his wealth. The salam buyer can either annul or take the kurr and give the heirs 60 dirhams.
The debt of 10 dirhams is owed to the salam buyer, but the buyer offers to forgo it in exchange for the kurr.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reasoning
Abu Hanifa: if the buyer takes the kurr, the separate legatee gets nothing. Reasoning: the mahaba (favor) is a bequest of the entire asset (90 out of 100), while the other bequest is only one-third (30). The free estate after debt is 90, and the one-third is 30. The mahaba claim of 90 is larger, so it takes full priority over the 30 claim.
The one-third limit applies to total bequests, but Abu Hanifa sees the mahaba as occupying the entire one-third.
3
State the two companions' position and reasoning
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: the two bequests share the one-third proportionally. The salam buyer claims 90, the other legatee claims 30. Total claims within the one-third = 120, but only 30 available. So they apply 'awl: 30 ÷ 120 = 1/4 per unit. The buyer gets 3/4 of 30 = 22.5; the other gets 1/4 of 30 = 7.5.
They treat both bequests as competing claims on the one-third, reducing each proportionally.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Abu Hanifa, the separate legatee receives nothing. Under the two, the separate legatee receives 7.5 dirhams (one-quarter of the one-third). The buyer's share differs: he gets the full kurr (worth 100) minus 60 to heirs = 40 net benefit under Abu Hanifa; under the two, he gets 22.5 from the one-third plus the retained capital? Actually the text says he pays 60 to heirs and takes kurr, so net = 100 - 60 = 40. Under the two, he would pay less to heirs? The text: 'وإن شاء أخذ الكر وأعطى الورثة ستين درهماً' - that's the same for both. The difference is in the legatee's share.
The dispute affects only the separate legatee at this stage.
5
Note the talil and its implications
The reasoning (ta'lil) revolves around whether the mahaba bequest is treated as a specific asset bequest (takes priority) or as a general claim on the one-third. This is a classic Hanafi usul dispute about the scope of specific bequests vs. fractional bequests.
Later Hanafi practice tends to follow Abu Hanifa in such cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو أسلم إلى مريض عشرة في كر قيمته مائة فقبض رأس المال وأنفقه ومات وقد أوصى بثلث ماله فإن شاء رب السلم نقض السلم وأخذ دراهمه ويجوز للآخر وصيته، وإن شاء أخذ الكر وأعطى الورثة ستين درهماً ولا شيء لصاحب الوصية في قول أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يتحاصان في الثلث يضرب فيه رب السلم بتسعين وصاحب الوصية بثلاثين وهو ثلث المال فيكون الثلث بينهما على أربعة فيأخذ رب السلم الكر ويؤدي سبعة وستين درهماً ونصف منها تسعة الثلث لصاحب الوصية. وتخريجه أن عند أبي حنيفة ربع المحاباة أولى من الوصية ومال الميت قيمته مائة إلا أن عشرة منها مشغولة بالدين فيبقى ماله الفارغ بين رب السلم والموصى له على أربعة لأن الوصية بالمحاباة وصية ماله وذلك بجميع تسعون والوصية الأخرى بالثلث وذلك ثلاثون فيقسم الثلث على سبيل العول عندهما على أربعة ثلاثة أرباعه لصاحب المحاباة وذلك ثلاث وعشرون ونصف وأربعة للموصى له الآخر. وإذا كان للمريض على رجلين كر حنطة يساوي ثلاثين ورأس ماله عشرة وأقالهما ومات أحدهما غائب قيل للحاضر ردَّ ثلاثة أعشار نصف رأس المال وذلك درهم ونصف وأد سبعة أعشار نصف الكر وذلك يساوي عشرة ونصف فإذا قدم الغائب جازت الإقالة في نصف الكر فيؤدي القادم نصف رأس المال حصته درهم ونصف وربع الكر قيمته سبعة دراهم ونصف، وترد الورثة على الحاضر الطعام الذي أخذوه قدر ثلثه من عشرة ونصف ويأخذون منه درهماً من رأس المال والثلث على سهمين والجميع على ستة للغائب فيطرح لأنه مستوفى وصيته بقي خمسة خمس للحاضر وأربعة للورثة فيكون للحاضر خمس ما عليه وعليه نصف كر قيمته خمسة عشر وخمس خمسة ثلاثة درهم فيكون له ثلاثة دراهم ثلاثة أعشار ثلث ماله فصحت الإقالة بقدر ثلاثة أعشار ثلث ماله فصحت الإقالة بقدر ثلاثة أعشار نصف الكر وذلك أربعة ونصف وبطلت في سبعة أعشار نصف الكر فيرد ذلك وقيمته عشرة ونصف إلا رهماً در ونصفا العوض ما أدى من درهم من رأس المال وثلاثة محاباة. وإذا ظهرت وصية الحاضر ثلاثة درهم ظهر أن وصية الغائب مثل ذلك فقد نفذنا الوصية في ستة وأعطينا الورثة ضعفها اثني عشر فقد استقام الثلث والثلثان، وإذا حضر الغائب فقد صحت الإقالة في نصف الكر.
If a person gives a sick person ten [dirhams] as salam for a kurr worth a hundred, and he takes the capital and spends it, and dies having bequeathed one-third of his wealth, then the salam buyer may annul and take his dirhams, and the other [legatee's] bequest is valid. If he chooses to take the kurr and give the heirs sixty dirhams, then according to Abu Hanifa, the other legatee gets nothing. According to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], they share proportionally in the one-third: the salam buyer claims ninety and the other legatee claims thirty – which is one-third of the wealth – so the one-third is divided between them into four parts: three-quarters for the salam buyer (twenty-three and a half) and one-quarter for the other legatee. The derivation: In Abu Hanifa's view, the mahaba bequest takes priority over the [separate] bequest. The deceased's wealth is worth a hundred, but ten is occupied by debt, so the free portion is between the salam buyer and the legatee into four parts, because the bequest by mahaba is a bequest of his wealth, totaling ninety, and the other bequest is one-third, totaling thirty, so the one-third is divided 'awl-fashion according to the two into four: three-quarters for the mahaba-holder (twenty-three and a half) and one-quarter for the other legatee. If a sick person is owed a kurr of wheat worth thirty by two men, his capital is ten, he cancels the debt for both, and one of them dies absent, it is said to the present one: return three-tenths of half the capital – that is one and a half dirhams – and pay seven-tenths of half the kurr, which is worth ten and a half. When the absent one returns, the cancellation is valid for half the kurr; the returning one pays half the capital, his share one and a half dirhams, and a quarter of the kurr worth seven and a half dirhams. The heirs return to the present one the food they took, one-third of ten and a half, and take from him a dirham from the capital. The one-third is on two shares, total six: for the absent one, it is dropped because he has received his bequest; remaining five: five for the present one and four for the heirs. So the present one owes one-fifth of what he owes: half a kurr worth fifteen, and one-fifth of five is three dirhams, so he owes three dirhams – three-tenths of one-third of his wealth. Thus the cancellation is valid for three-tenths of one-third of his wealth, i.e., three-tenths of half the kurr, which is four and a half, and invalid for seven-tenths of half the kurr, so that is returned, its value ten and a half except a dirham and a half – the compensation for what he paid from the capital and three favor. If the present one's bequest appears as three dirhams, and the absent one's bequest likewise, then we have executed the bequest in six and given the heirs twice that, twelve, so the one-third and two-thirds are correct. When the absent one returns, the cancellation is valid for half the kurr.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the prioritization of bequests when a salam buyer's mahaba (favor) competes with a separate bequest of one-third. Abu Hanifa holds that the mahaba bequest takes full priority over the one-third bequest, so the separate legatee receives nothing if the buyer chooses to proceed. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue for proportional allocation (muhasat) within the one-third, giving the salam buyer three-quarters and the other legatee one-quarter. The passage then transitions to a complex scenario involving two debtors, cancellation of debt (iqlah), and the calculation of valid portions. This scenario illustrates how the principles apply when one debtor is absent and his bequest is discovered later. The calculations involve determining the valid portion of the cancellation based on the one-third limit, with the absent debtor's bequest affecting the distribution.

Key Terms
العول (al-ʿawl): Proportional reduction of shares when the sum of fixed shares exceeds the whole.
الإقالة (al-iqālah): Rescission of a sale or contract by mutual agreement.
المحاباة (al-muhābāh): A favor in pricing, selling below market value; considered a bequest of the difference.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Both bequests are invalid.
B) The separate legatee gets the entire one-third.
C) The salam buyer gets the entire one-third, and the separate legatee gets nothing.
D) They share the one-third proportionally.

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute over competing bequests, Abu Hanifa gives full priority to a specific asset bequest (mahaba) over a fractional one-third bequest, while the two companions apply proportional reduction.

Will for Manumission of Unspecified Slave with Money: From Fatawa al-Fadli
Ruling on will for manumission of unspecified slave with money bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on a bequest of money to an unspecified manumitted slave, distinguishing when such a bequest is valid and when it requires a discretionary phrase.

Core Idea
A bequest of money to an unspecified freed slave is invalid unless the testator gives the executor discretion.

Fatawa al-Fadli presents a nuanced scenario: a testator bequeaths both the manumission of his slave woman and a gift of money to her. The ruling depends on whether the slave is specifically identified or not, and whether the testator uses a phrase that grants the executor discretion. This lesson unpacks the conditions for validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two parts of the bequest
The testator makes two bequests: manumission (عتق) and a gift of money (مال). Each has its own ruling.
2
Check if the slave is specified
If the slave is specified (معينة) by name or clear description, both bequests are valid separately. If unspecified, only the manumission is valid by default.
Specified means the slave is identified such that the bequest is not ambiguous.
3
Evaluate the money bequest for an unspecified slave
If the slave is unspecified, the money bequest is invalid unless the testator adds a discretionary phrase (تخيير) like 'I have made it such that if he wishes, he gives to the one he manumits'.
This phrase transforms the bequest into a valid discretionary will, similar to entrusting one-third to the executor.
4
Note the variant about selling the slave
If the testator bequeaths that his slave be sold to someone he loves, the heir has the option to sell to whomever he wishes; if the intended buyer refuses the full price, the price is reduced by one-third.
5
Apply the ruling to new scenarios
Use the conditions above to determine validity in similar bequests to unspecified beneficiaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتاوى الفضلي : أوصى بعتق أمه وأن يعطي لها بعد ثلث ماله كذا قال : إن كانت الأمة معينة جازت لها الوصية بالعتق وبالمال جميعاً، وإن كانت بغير عينها جازت الوصية بالعتق ولا تجوز الوصية بالمال إلا أن يقول جعلت ذلك إن أحب أعطى التي أعتقها فيكون ذلك وصية جائزة كقوله ضع ثلث مالي مفوضاً إلى الوصي أنه لو أوصى أن تباع أمته ممن أحب جاز ويخير الوارث على أن يبيعها حيث شئت ألا تری ممن أحب، وإن أبى ذلك الرجل أن يشتريها بقيمتها حط عن قيمتها مقدار ثلث ما للموصي .
And in Fatawa al-Fadli: He bequeathed the manumission of his slave woman and that she be given after one-third of his wealth such and such. He said: If the slave woman is specific, the will for manumission and for money is valid together. And if she is unspecified, the will for manumission is valid and the will for money is not valid, unless he says: 'I have made that such that if he wishes, he gives to the one he manumits,' then that is a valid will, like his saying: 'Place my third entrusted to the executor.' Also, if he bequeaths that his slave woman be sold to whomever he loves, it is valid, and the heir may choose to sell her wherever he wishes, or if that man refuses to buy her at her value, the amount equal to one-third of the testator's wealth is deducted from her value.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This fatwa from Fatawa al-Fadli addresses a situation where a testator bequeaths both the manumission of his slave woman and a gift of money to her from the remaining two-thirds. The key distinction is whether the slave woman is specifically identified (معينة) or not. If she is identified by name, both the manumission and the money bequest are valid as separate wills, each subject to the one-third rule. If she is not specified (e.g., 'a slave woman'), the will for manumission is valid (the executor chooses which slave), but the money bequest is not valid because it is a bequest to an unspecified person. However, if the testator says: 'I leave it to the executor to give if he wishes to the one he manumits,' then it becomes a valid discretionary will (تخيير), like entrusting the third to the executor. The fatwa also discusses a variant: if the testator bequeaths that his slave woman be sold to someone he loves, the heir has the option to sell to whomever he wishes; if the preferred buyer refuses to pay the full value, the slave's price can be reduced by one-third to facilitate the sale.

Key Terms
معينة (mu'ayyanah): A specific, identified slave; here, the slave is named or clearly described.
تخيير (takhyīr): Discretion given to the executor; here, the testator gives the executor choice to give money to the manumitted slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) If the heirs agree
D) If the slave is a relative

Key Takeaway
A bequest of money to an unspecified manumitted slave is invalid unless the testator explicitly grants the executor discretion (takhyeer) to give it.

Judge's Investigation and Surety Requirement for Claim on Absentee's Property
Judge's procedure with claimant without evidence, including delay and surety requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the judge's procedure when a claimant without evidence is confirmed by the holder, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on taking a surety, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The judge must delay and investigate, then may require a surety from the claimant before handing over property to protect absent heirs.

This lesson examines the first scenario from the passage: a claimant appears without evidence, but the property holder confirms the claim. The judge does not rule immediately. Instead, he delays (talawwum) and investigates for potential heirs. If none appear, he may order payment but requires a surety (kafil) from the claimant. There is a known difference between Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn on whether a surety is required. This lesson clarifies the procedure and the preferred Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the holder's confirmation
Read the part where a claimant has no evidence but the holder confirms the claim. Note that the holder may be holding the property as trust, debt, usurpation, or bequest. The claimant's admission about an heir determines the judge's response.
2
Understand the judge's duty to delay and investigate (talawwum)
The judge must not rush. He waits for a period, allowing potential heirs or other claimants to come forward. This is a key principle in Hanafi procedural law to protect absentee rights.
3
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute on taking a surety
After the delay, if no heir appears, the judge orders payment. There is a difference: Abu Hanifa does not require a surety, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require a reliable surety from the claimant. Some scholars say this dispute is agreed (ittifaq).
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later Hanafi authorities (like Al-Marghinani) prefer the cautious view: the judge should take a surety. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Apply the ruling to a new case
If the claimant is confirmed but admits the owner may have an absent heir, the judge delays even longer. The surety protects the absent heir if he appears later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا باب العتق في المرض والوصية بالعتق
إلى صدر المسألة فقال : لو أن الموصى له أقام البينة أن فلاناً مات ولم يدع وارثاً وأوصى إليه بالألف التي قبل فلان وقال الشهود لا نعلم له وارثاً والذي قبله المال مقر بالمال الذي قبله فالقاضي يقضي بالمال للموصى له قال محمد في الجامع رجل ألف درهم دين أو كان الألف في يده غصباً أو وديعة أو كانت الألف فهذا فغاب صاحب المال فقام رجلا وادعى أن صاحب المال أوصى له بهذا الألف الذي قبل هذا الرجل ولا بينة له فصدقه الذي قبله المال فهذا على وجهين : أما إن أقر المدعي أن لصاحب المال وارثاً غائباً أو قال لا أدري أله وارث أم لا، أو قال المدعي ليس لصاحب المال وارث. وإن كان صاحب المال رجلاً نصرانياً أسلم ولم يترك أحداً وصدقه الذي قبله المال في ذلك ففي الوجه الأول القاضي لا يقضي على الذي في يديه المال في الوجوه الأربعة الغصب والوديعة والدين والإيصاء إلا أن القاضي يتلوم في ذلك ويتأنى ولا يعجل، فإن جاء مدع أو وارث وإلا قضى القاضي بالمال للمدعي، وإن كان المال وديعة عند رجل كان له أن يضمن القابض بإجماع. وهل له أن يضمن المودع؟ فعل قول محمد رحمه الله كان له ذلك، وعلى قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله ليس له ذلك. وإن كان المال ديناً فلصاحب المال أن يضمن الغريم وليس له أن يضمن القابض، وإن ضمن الغريم كان للغريم أن يرجع على القابض .
وأما إذا كان المال وصل إليه من قبل أبيه أوصى إليه أبوه وصورة هذا وتفسيره إذا كان الرجل ألف درهم دفعها إلى رجل وجعله وصياً فيه ثم مات الموصى له فوصل المال إلى ابن الموصي من جهة أبيه الذي كان أوصى بها إلى ابنه وكان في يديه فدفع إلى هذا المدعي بأمر القاضي. ثم جاء صاحب المال حياً ولكن حضر وارثه فأقام البينة أنه أخوه من أبيه وأمه لا وارث له غيره فلا ضمان على الذي قبله المال في الوجوه كلها وأن الذي في يده المال أقر أن هذا أخ صاحب المال وأنه قد مات إلا أني لا أدري أهذا وارثه أم لا لم يقض القاضي في ذلك زماناً فلم يظهر له وارث آخر ودفع المقر المال إلى المقر له بأمر القاضي ثم جاء صاحب المال حياً قال محمد في الكتاب : فهو بمنزلة الموصى له في جميع ما وصفت لك في حق التضمين ولو بقي صاحب المال حياً لكن جاء رجل وأقام البينة أنه ابنه قال في الكتاب : هذا بمنزلة الموصى له في جميع ما وصفت لك في أنه لا ضمان على الذي قبله المال في الفصول كلها، وأن الضمان على القابض. ولو أن الذي في يده المال أقر لرجل أنه ابن الميت وأن للميت ابناً آخر وقال الابن المقر له ليس له ابن آخر تلوم القاضي زماناً، وإذا تلوم زماناً ولم يحضر وارث آخر دفع المال كله إليه. ثم قال في الكتاب : إذا تلوم القاضي زماناً ولم يظهر للميت ابن آخر أمر القاضي الذي قبله المال أن يدفع المال كله إلى المدعي ويأخذ منه كفيلاً ثقة، وما لم يعطه كفيلاً ثقة لا يدفع المال نظراً للغائب لجواز أن يكون للميت ابن آخر، فمن مشايخنا من قال : هذا قولهما. أما على قول أبي حنيفة لا يأخذ كفيلاً. وقال بعض المشايخ : لا بل هذا على الاتفاق، فإن جاء وارث آخر فلا ضمان على الذي قبله المال في الوجوه كلها، ولكن الضمان على القابض وكفيله ولو كان الذي حضر ادعى أن له على صاحب درهم دین وأنه مات فصدقه الذي قبله المال في ذلك لم يلتفت القاضي إلى ذلك ولم يجعل بينهما خصومة حتى يحضر الوارث في الوجوه الأربعة. وهذا إذا أنكر المدعي أن للميت وراثاً وقال لا أدري له وراثاً أم لا، فإن أقر الذي قبله المال والمدعي أنه ليس له وراث فالقاضي يتلوم ويتأنى زماناً، ثم إذا تلوم زماناً ولم يظهر له وارث فالقاضي لا يدفع المال إلى المقر ولكن ينصب لنصيب الميت وصياً ليستوفي مال الميت على الناس ويوفي ما على الميت للناس. وإذا نصب يأمر المدعي بإقامة البينة على الوصي، فإن أقام البينة على هذا الوصي . القاضي الوصي بأن يدفع حقه إليه وإذا دفع ثم جاء صاحب المال حياً والمال مستهلك عند المقر له كان الجواب في الوجوه كلها الأربعة الوديعة والدين والغصب والأيصاء كما قلنا في الفصل الأول. ولو لم يجئ صاحب المال حياً لكن حضر وارثه وجحد الدين لم يلتفت إلى جحوده وكان قضاء القاضي ماضياً ولا يكلف المدعي المدين إقامة البينة على الوارث. وقال في الجامع الصغير : رجل له وديعة أو غصب أو دين عليه فجاء رجل وأقام البينة أن صاحب المال قد توفي وهذا المدعي أخوه لأبيه وأمه ووارثه لا وارث له غيره والذي قبله المال جاحد للمال أو مقر بالمال منكر لما سواه فالمدعى عليه خصم له فإذا قضى القاضي له بالمال كله فقبضه ثم جاء صاحب المال حياً وقد هلك في يد القابض فإن كان الذي عنده غاصباً فصاحب المال بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الشهود وإن شاء ضمن الغاصب وإن شاء ضمن الأخ، فإن اختار تضمين الغاصب كان الغاصب بالخيار، وإن شاء ضمن الشهود ورجعوا على الأخ، وإن شاء ضمن الأخ ، لا يرجع على أحد ولا يرجع على الشهود وإن كان الذي عليه المال مودوعاً فلا ضمان لصاحب المال على الشهود، فإذا أخذ صاحب المال الدين من الغريم كان الغريم بالخيار إن شاء ضمن الشاهدين أو ضمن الأخ فإن ضمن الشهود رجعوا على الأخ، وإن ضمن الأخ لا يرجع على الشهود ولو لم يأت صاحب المال حياً فلا يتحقق موته كما شهدت الشهود فجاء رجل وأقام بينة أني ابن الميت قضى القاضي بذلك فلا ضمان على الدافع في الوجوه كلها ولكن الابن مخير إن شاء ضمن الشهود وإن شاء ضمن الأخ. فإن ضمن الأخ لم يرجع على الشهود وإن ضمن الشهود رجعوا على الأخ. ولو لم يقم الثاني بينة أنه ابن الميت لكنه أقام بينة أن أخو الميت لأبيه وأمه ووارثه قضى القاضي ببينته ويقضي القاضي له بنصف ما قبض الأول من الميراث ولا ضمان على الذي قبله المال في الصور كلها
ولا ضمان على الشهود هنا .
قال رحمه الله: (ولو) ادعى رجل ديناً والعبد عتقاً وصدقهما الوارث سعى في قيمته
Book of Wills, Chapter on Manumission during Illness and Bequest of Manumission. Up to the beginning of the issue, he said: If the legatee establishes evidence that so-and-so died and left no heir, and bequeathed to him the thousand that is with so-and-so, and the witnesses say we know of no heir for him, and the one with whom the property is acknowledges the property that is with him, then the judge rules the property for the legatee. Muhammad said in al-Jami: A man has a debt of one thousand dirhams, or the thousand is in his hand as a usurpation or a trust, or the thousand is such, and the owner of the property goes absent, then a man stands up and claims that the owner of the property bequeathed to him this thousand that is with this man, and he has no evidence, and the one with whom the property is confirms him. This is in two aspects: Either the claimant admits that the owner of the property has an absent heir, or he says I do not know if he has an heir or not, or the claimant says the owner of the property has no heir. And if the owner of the property was a Christian man who became Muslim and left no one, and the one with whom the property is confirms him in that, then in the first aspect the judge does not rule against the one in whose hand the property is in the four types: usurpation, trust, debt, and bequest, except that the judge investigates and waits and does not hasten. If a claimant or heir comes, otherwise the judge rules the property for the claimant. And if the property is a trust with a man, it is his option to hold the receiver liable by consensus. Is it his option to hold the trustee liable? According to the statement of Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, he may do so; according to the statement of Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, he may not. If the property is a debt, the owner of the property may hold the debtor liable, and he may not hold the receiver liable. If he holds the debtor liable, the debtor may recourse against the receiver. As for if the property reached him by way of his father, his father bequeathed to him—the picture and explanation of this is: if a man had one thousand dirhams that he gave to another man and made him an executor over it, then the legatee died, so the property reached the son of the testator by way of his father who had bequeathed it to his son, and it was in his hand, and he gave it to this claimant by order of the judge. Then the owner of the property came alive, but his heir appeared and established evidence that he is his brother from father and mother, and he has no other heir. Then there is no liability on the one with whom the property was in all the categories, and that the one in whose hand the property was acknowledged that this is the brother of the owner of the property and that he had died, but I do not know if he is his heir or not; the judge did not rule on that for a time, and no other heir appeared, and the acknowledger gave the property to the acknowledged one by order of the judge, then the owner of the property came alive. Muhammad said in the book: it is like the legatee in all that I described to you regarding liability. Even if the owner of the property remained alive, but a man came and established evidence that he is his son. He said in the book: this is like the legatee in all that I described to you in that there is no liability on the one with whom the property was in all the chapters, and that liability is on the receiver. And if the one in whose hand the property was acknowledged to a man that he is the son of the deceased and that the deceased has another son, and the acknowledged son said he has no other son, the judge investigates for a time. When he investigates for a time and no other heir appears, he gives all the property to him. Then he said in the book: when the judge investigates for a time and no other son of the deceased appears, he orders the one with whom the property is to give all the property to the claimant and take from him a reliable surety. As long as he does not give a reliable surety, he does not give the property, looking out for the absent one because it is possible that the deceased has another son. Some of our teachers said: this is their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) opinion. According to the opinion of Abu Hanifa, he does not take a surety. And some teachers said: no, rather this is by agreement. If another heir comes, there is no liability on the one with whom the property was in all the categories, but liability is on the receiver and his surety. And if the one who appeared claimed that he has a debt against the owner of the dirham and that he died, and the one with whom the property was confirmed him in that, the judge does not pay attention to that and does not make a case between them until the heir appears in the four types. This is if the claimant denies that the deceased has an heir and says I do not know if he has an heir or not. If the one with whom the property was and the claimant both acknowledge that he has no heir, the judge investigates and waits for a time. Then when he investigates for a time and no heir appears, the judge does not give the property to the acknowledger but appoints an executor for the share of the deceased to collect the property of the deceased from people and pay what is owed by the deceased to people. When he appoints, he orders the claimant to establish evidence before the executor. If he establishes evidence before this executor, the judge orders the executor to give his right to him. When he gives and then the owner of the property comes alive and the property is consumed with the acknowledged one, the answer in all the four categories—trust, debt, usurpation, and bequest—is as we said in the first chapter. And if the owner of the property does not come alive but his heir appears and denies the debt, his denial is not heeded and the judge's ruling is effective, and the claimant is not required to establish evidence against the heir. And he said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: A man has a trust, or a usurpation, or a debt upon him, then a man comes and establishes evidence that the owner of the property has died and this claimant is his brother from father and mother and his heir, and he has no other heir, and the one with whom the property is either denies the property or acknowledges the property but denies what is besides it. Then the defendant is a valid opponent. When the judge rules for him all the property and he takes it, then the owner of the property comes alive and it perishes in the hand of the receiver. If the one who had it was a usurper, the owner of the property has a choice: if he wishes, he may hold the witnesses liable; if he wishes, he may hold the usurper liable; if he wishes, he may hold the brother liable. If he chooses to hold the usurper liable, the usurper has a choice; if he wishes, he may hold the witnesses liable, and they recourse against the brother; if he wishes, he may hold the brother liable, and the brother does not recourse against anyone, nor does he recourse against the witnesses. If the one upon whom the property was is a trustee, then the owner of the property has no liability against the witnesses. So if the owner of the property takes the debt from the debtor, the debtor has a choice: if he wishes, he may hold the two witnesses liable, or he may hold the brother liable. If he holds the witnesses liable, they recourse against the brother; if he holds the brother liable, he does not recourse against the witnesses. And if the owner of the property does not come alive, so his death is not verified as the witnesses testified, then a man comes and establishes evidence that he is the son of the deceased; the judge rules on that. Then there is no liability on the one who paid in all the categories, but the son has a choice: if he wishes, he may hold the witnesses liable; if he wishes, he may hold the brother liable. If he holds the brother liable, he does not recourse against the witnesses; if he holds the witnesses liable, they recourse against the brother. And if the second does not establish evidence that he is the son of the deceased, but he establishes evidence that he is the brother of the deceased from father and mother and his heir, the judge rules on his evidence, and the judge rules for him half of what the first took from the inheritance, and there is no liability on the one with whom the property was in all the forms, and there is no liability on the witnesses here. He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (And if) a man claims a debt and the slave's manumission, and the heir confirms both, he strives for its value.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the rulings of claims to property when the owner is absent or deceased and no heir is known. It addresses multiple scenarios involving property held as trust, debt, usurpation, or bequest, and the procedure for a judge when a claimant comes forward with or without evidence. The passage opens by discussing a case where a legatee (al-mūṣā lahu) provides evidence of a bequest and the holder acknowledges, leading the judge to rule in the legatee's favor. Then it transitions to a scenario from Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' where a man has property (debt, trust, etc.) and the owner becomes absent; a claimant appears without evidence but is confirmed by the holder. The ruling distinguishes two possibilities: either the claimant admits there may be an absent heir, says he does not know, or denies any heir. In the first case, the judge delays, investigates, and does not rule immediately. If no heir appears, the judge eventually rules for the claimant. The text then details differences between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf regarding whether the owner can hold the trustee liable. For trust property, there is consensus that the owner can hold the receiver (qābiḍ) liable; but Muhammad allows holding the trustee (mūdiʿ) liable, while Abu Yusuf does not. For debt, the owner can hold the debtor liable but not the receiver. Next, a scenario where the property reached the claimant via his father's bequest: the holder paid by judge's order, then the original owner appears alive. Here, no liability falls on the holder; the liability is on the receiver (qābiḍ) if the property is lost. The same applies if a son appears after the property was paid. The passage then discusses taking a surety (kafil) from the claimant: the judge orders the holder to take a reliable surety before handing over property, to protect potential absent heirs. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Some scholars attribute this requirement to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, while Abu Hanifa reportedly does not require a surety. Others say it is agreed upon. If a subsequent heir appears, the holder is not liable; liability is on the receiver and his surety. The text further discusses cases where the claimant claims a debt against the deceased, and the holder confirms but the judge does not proceed until the heir appears. If both holder and claimant agree there is no heir, the judge investigates, and if no heir appears, the judge appoints an executor (waṣī) to handle the estate; the claimant must prove his claim before the executor. If the owner then returns alive and the property is consumed, the ruling is as before. If the heir appears and denies the debt, the judge's previous ruling is effective. The passage concludes with cases from al-Jami' al-Saghir: if a person has a trust, etc., and a claimant proves he is the brother and heir, the judge rules for him; later the owner appears alive and the property is lost. The owner has options to hold witnesses, the usurper, or the brother liable, with various recourse possibilities. If the owner does not appear, and a second claimant appears as son, the judge rules for him; no liability on the holder. The son may hold witnesses or the first recipient liable. If the second claimant proves he is a brother, he gets half the inheritance. The passage ends with a new ruling: if a man claims both a debt and the manumission of a slave, and the heir confirms both, the slave strives for his value. This expansion of the matn clarifies the procedures and liabilities in complex property claims, emphasizing the judge's precautionary role and the protection of absentee heirs.

Key Terms
القابض (al-qābiḍ): The person who receives the property from the holder, i.e., the claimant or his agent who takes possession.
التلوم (al-talawwum): The judge's act of waiting and investigating for a period of time before ruling, to allow potential heirs or claimants to appear.
الكفيل (al-kafil): A surety or guarantor who undertakes to compensate if the claimant's claim is later found invalid or if an heir appears.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a claimant without evidence is confirmed by the holder, and the claimant admits the deceased may have an absent heir, what is the judge's immediate duty?
A) Immediately rule the property to the claimant
B) Reject the claim due to lack of evidence
C) Delay and investigate (talawwum) before ruling
D) Order the holder to pay but take a surety immediately

Key Takeaway
When a claim to a deceased's property is unproven but confirmed by the holder, the judge must delay, investigate, and then (according to the mufta bihi) require a surety before handing over the property to protect potential absent heirs.

Liability Options After Property Paid by Court Order
Owner's options to hold parties liable after property paid by court order, with recourse details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the parties that can be held liable when the original owner returns after property has been paid by court order, and apply the Hanafi rules on recourse among them.

Core Idea
When the original owner returns alive after the property is paid, he may hold liable either the witnesses, the wrongful holder (usurper), or the receiver, with specific recourse rules.

This lesson examines the second major part of the passage: after the judge has ruled and the property has been paid to the claimant, the original owner may appear alive. The text explains the options (takhyir) available to the owner depending on how the property was held originally (trust, debt, usurpation). It also details the rights of recourse among the parties. Understanding these options is critical for a judge or mufti advising on liability in complex property claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the post-payment scenario
Read the part beginning from al-Jami' al-Saghir: after the judge rules and the property is handed over, the original owner appears alive and the property is lost (perished) in the hands of the receiver.
2
Classify the original holding
Determine whether the property was held as a trust, debt, or usurpation. Each triggers different liability rules.
3
List the owner's options for each type
For usurpation: owner may hold witnesses, the usurper, or the receiver (brother) liable. For trust: owner cannot hold witnesses liable but may hold the debtor or receiver. For debt: similar to trust with variations.
4
Trace the recourse among parties
If the owner holds one party, that party may have recourse against another. For example, the usurper may recourse against witnesses or the brother. The brother (receiver) does not recourse against anyone.
5
Apply to a scenario with no return of owner
If the owner does not appear, but a second heir appears, the second heir also has options to hold parties liable, with similar recourse rules.
